              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2018">read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=books-owned-all-formats">books-owned-all-formats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-atoz2018">challenge-atoz2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579388933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer861242967304964528">Imagine a book that is a mystery with the sensibility of a gothic horror but is also a story about loyalty and friendships, and love and betrayal. How can one book be so many things and not feel like a gigantic mess? Well in the hands of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/815.Carlos_Ruiz_Zaf_n' title='Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carlos Ruiz Zafón</a> it seems such feats are indeed possible. <br/><br/>'The Angel's Game' is the second book in his <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/72526-el-cementerio-de-los-libros-olvidados' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cemetery of Forgotten Book</a> series following on from my much loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1461877448?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a>. But it's not a direct sequel. It's a prequel but can very much b</span>
  <span id="freeText861242967304964528" style="display:none">Imagine a book that is a mystery with the sensibility of a gothic horror but is also a story about loyalty and friendships, and love and betrayal. How can one book be so many things and not feel like a gigantic mess? Well in the hands of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/815.Carlos_Ruiz_Zaf_n" title="Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">Carlos Ruiz Zafón</a> it seems such feats are indeed possible. <br /><br />'The Angel's Game' is the second book in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/72526-el-cementerio-de-los-libros-olvidados" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cemetery of Forgotten Book</a> series following on from my much loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1461877448?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a>. But it's not a direct sequel. It's a prequel but can very much be read as a standalone. <br /><br />I don't know how to explain the storyline other than to say I was entirely captivated. I never for one second knew where the plot would twist and turn to next. These are truly books for book-lovers. Whereas Shadow explored a love for books more from a reader's vantage this one touches on the love a writer has for the written word. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I had always felt that the pages I left behind were a part of me. Normal people bring children into the world; we novelists bring books. We are condemned to put our whole lives into them, even though they hardly ever thank us for it. We are condemned to die in their pages and sometimes even to let our books be the ones who, in the end, will take our lives.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />As with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> the quality of the writing is of the highest calibre. The streets of Barcelona truly come alive in the pages of this book as do the colourful, larger than life characters who inhabit them. <br /><br />My absolute favourite thing about this book was the relationship between David and Isabella. It was so gloriously written. They perfectly complimented each other in their roles as mentor and student and the true friendship that blossomed between them is one of the most beautiful connections between two people that I've ever read.<br /><br />Admittedly this book doesn't quite reach the perfection of its published precursor as the ending is a little more hurried than I would like but it makes for an absolutely rip-roaring of a read. And reading this has made me incredibly excited to read book three in the series. <br /><br /><b>four stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="861242967304964528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2484072266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484072266" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484072266?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/52941093-the-angel-s-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484072266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3531195547147869955"><strong><i>The Angel's Game</i> was equally as spellbinding and bewitching as <em>The Shadow of the Wind</em>, but in a totally different way.</strong><br/><br/>While <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> narrated a captivating story from the perspective of a reader, this book took a more disturbing and sinister path into the mind of a writer. The timeline of <i>The Angel's Game</i> took place before the events of the first book; a prequel that was about David Martìn; a devastatingly tragic story about a broken character who was a brilliant but misconstrued w</span>
  <span id="freeText3531195547147869955" style="display:none"><strong><i>The Angel's Game</i> was equally as spellbinding and bewitching as <em>The Shadow of the Wind</em>, but in a totally different way.</strong><br /><br />While <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> narrated a captivating story from the perspective of a reader, this book took a more disturbing and sinister path into the mind of a writer. The timeline of <i>The Angel's Game</i> took place before the events of the first book; a prequel that was about David Martìn; a devastatingly tragic story about a broken character who was a brilliant but misconstrued writer. David was a complex, compelling, and immensely sympathetic character. However, compared to Daniel Sempere, the main protagonist from the first book, David could not exactly be considered as a nice person. Having said that, he was the product of a harsh environment and depressing life experiences which I wouldn't wish on anyone. My heart totally ached for him as I was held spellbound by his story.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"The only way you can truly get to know an author is through the trail of ink he leaves behind him; the person you think you see is only an empty character: truth is always hidden in fiction."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />The disturbing and sinister part of his tale comes from what appears to be a descent into madness in David's mind, of which I wouldn't elaborate too much to avoid spoilers. It was a brilliant move to tell his story from a first person perspective as David represents the quintessential unreliable narrator. As a reader, the lines between reality, memory, dreams and imagination slowly but surely became indistinguishable. The realisation of this though didn't happen till pretty late in the book (for me anyway), which made the reading experience absolutely mesmerizing. Given this, the setting in <i>The Angel's Game</i> took on an even more gothic feel that bordered on the supernatural. There were certain scenes which outright sent shivers down my spine.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"I stepped into the bookshop and breathed in that perfume of paper and magic that strangely no one had ever though of bottling."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />Just as in the first book, Sempere &amp; Sons, the bookshop remained as an important highlight of the story, as was the Cemetery of Forgotten Books itself. The Sempere family and their bookshop formed the sole source of comfort in David's life. The wholesome goodness of the Sempere family and the magic of books permeated these pages, granting the reader the much needed reprieve from the unrelenting doom and gloom of David's story.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"Poetry is written with tears, novels with blood, and history with invisible ink."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />All the above already made for great storytelling, but what made these books even more incredible was the writing. I can't read Spanish so I wouldn't be able to tell how accurate or faithful the translation was, but what I could say was that it was phenomenal. I do believe that it's both the original writing and the translation together that made the prose so beautiful. There's simply no other way to describe it. Even in its darkest note, and there're plenty in this particular volume, there is an undeniable and sublime beauty in the music of the prose.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"We think we understand a song's lyrics, but what makes us believe in them, or not, is the music."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />I think this series will become one of my all-time favourites if the quality of the prose, its engaging and emotionally powerful storytelling continue with the last two books. <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> felt like a stand-alone story. But once you've read <i>The Angel's Game</i>, there's no turning back from reading the rest as it promises so much more to come. <br /><br /><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Angels-Game-Carlos-Ruiz-Zafon/9780753826492/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u> | <u><a href="https://bookshop.org/books/the-angel-s-game-a-psychological-thriller/9780767931113" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookshop.org</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-1Tz" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and my other reviews at <a href="http://novelnotions.net/category/book-reviews/tss-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3531195547147869955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125881757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125881757" />
    <a title="Yzobelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3745601-yzobelle"><img alt="Yzobelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397879180p2/3745601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125881757?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yzobelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yzobelle" href="/user/show/3745601-yzobelle">Yzobelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780767931113" href="/book/show/7380399-the-angel-s-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3745601-yzobelle?shelf=for-sharing-at-blink">for-sharing-at-blink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3745601-yzobelle?shelf=to-read-again">to-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125881757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer858361860612186784">Once more, Zafon takes his readers to a thrilling ride into a web of stories. And any ride with Zafon is guaranteed to be breathtaking.<br/><br/>In the Angel's Game, Zafon has again exhibited his specialty in leading his readers into a series of intricate stories. He makes sure his readers enter that labyrinth of events so engrossed that they would hardly feel that they have been sucked into it. But great Zafon makes sure that his readers come out of it safe. He really has that talent of giving little une</span>
  <span id="freeText858361860612186784" style="display:none">Once more, Zafon takes his readers to a thrilling ride into a web of stories. And any ride with Zafon is guaranteed to be breathtaking.<br /><br />In the Angel's Game, Zafon has again exhibited his specialty in leading his readers into a series of intricate stories. He makes sure his readers enter that labyrinth of events so engrossed that they would hardly feel that they have been sucked into it. But great Zafon makes sure that his readers come out of it safe. He really has that talent of giving little unexpected twists here and there while ending the whole story with one big unforeseen twist. <br /><br />The ride through the whole book is something to be cherished. He successfully puts his readers under his spell -- playing with their emotions through his sarcastic humor, manly ego, proud wit, writer's vanity, and pure friendship. <br /><br />There is so much wisdom in Zafon's words, through Sempere the bookseller: "Every book has a soul, the soul of the person who wrote it, and of those who read it and dream about it."<br /><br />Am sure Angel's Game, Shadow of the Wind, and even The Prince of Mist will be the content of my dreams for quite a long time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="858361860612186784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review125881757">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3407432200" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12902923383059534122">4.5 STARS<br/><br/>The Angel's Game is like a tea kettle over a fire, its tension bubbling and brewing before exploding into something you'll never forget. This story took me on a journey and I absolutely sped through it all, wondering what would happen next. Normally, I'm intimidated by books over 500 pages because I hate committing to such a long story (in my eyes), but I fell headfirst into this novel that is so intricate and mind-boggling, I keep questioning why someone hasn't adapted this into a film</span>
  <span id="freeText12902923383059534122" style="display:none">4.5 STARS<br /><br />The Angel's Game is like a tea kettle over a fire, its tension bubbling and brewing before exploding into something you'll never forget. This story took me on a journey and I absolutely sped through it all, wondering what would happen next. Normally, I'm intimidated by books over 500 pages because I hate committing to such a long story (in my eyes), but I fell headfirst into this novel that is so intricate and mind-boggling, I keep questioning why someone hasn't adapted this into a film yet. It's practically made to be a movie with its large cast of characters backdropped in the darkest parts of Spain following an author who gets too deep into an opportunity that threatens his life and the lives of those around him. <br /><br />Carlos Ruiz Zafon leaves me in awe of his ability to paint a scene so vividly, playing with words like an instrument, causing me to highlight passage after passage because the way he structures his sentences is an absolute work of art that I can admire for hours. <br /><br />While this story wasn't as intriguing, for me, as The Shadow of the Wind, that's not to say it wasn't absolutely amazing in its ability to be a wonderous historical fiction mixed with a psychological thriller. I'm so glad I finally picked this up because it quickly became one of my favorite reads of 2020. If only I had the ability and the craft to write a story as beautifully as Zafon did. May he rest in peace. <br /><br />CONTENT WARNINGS<br />Domestic abuse, tumors, fire, gun violence, self-harm, murder, death of an animal</span>

<div id="review_381789664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381789664" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9255064-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544028570p2/9255064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381789664?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9255064-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer381789664&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381789664" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15814941362994881062">It's hard for me to review Zafon's work, because I love it so much. I see the flaws in this novel, it may be a bit too wordy and the plot becomes convoluted in the second half, but I still loved it. Set in the Early 20th century in Barcelona, The Angel’s Game precedes the events in Zafon’s novel, The Shadow of the Wind, but shares a few of the same characters. David Martin is a poor journalist writing pulp fiction on the side, but he dreams of doing something greater. <br/><br/>Zafon’s style of writing ju</span>
  <span id="freeText15814941362994881062" style="display:none">It's hard for me to review Zafon's work, because I love it so much. I see the flaws in this novel, it may be a bit too wordy and the plot becomes convoluted in the second half, but I still loved it. Set in the Early 20th century in Barcelona, The Angel’s Game precedes the events in Zafon’s novel, The Shadow of the Wind, but shares a few of the same characters. David Martin is a poor journalist writing pulp fiction on the side, but he dreams of doing something greater. <br /><br />Zafon’s style of writing just drips with gorgeous descriptions, devious characters and tragic heroes. His gothic tales are so rich I am willing to forgive much that I would fault another author for. Like so many others, I didn't love this book as much as I loved The Shadow of the Wind, but again, I still loved it. Zafon has a few themes he always returns to in his work: the relationships between fathers and sons, men falling in love women in a higher social class, references to classic novels (Great Expectations, The Count of Monte Cristo), etc. This novel is no exception and it includes all of those things. <br /><br />**SPOILERS: Where I discuss my thoughts on Andreas Corelli**<br /><br />This year I re-read both Shadow of the Wind and this book and I’ve found that re-reading Zafon’s work is a lot like re-watching The Sixth Sense, once you know the ending you view the whole thing through a different lens. There’s one section where David meets Andreas Corelli and Corelli talks about his strained relationship with his father. He said he was cast out of his home and I couldn’t help thinking this was a clever reference to his father being “God” and Corelli being the Devil. <br /><br />Also, I forgot quite a bit about the details of David’s brain tumor. The most fascinating thing about this book is its ambiguity. For some it’s clear Corelli is the Devil and Martin makes a Faustian deal for both his health and what his soul desires. For others Martin is clearly a victim of his own delusions, brought on by his brain tumor. It’s possible his hallucinations are caused by schizophrenia or his brain tumor and the entire character of Corelli exists only in his mind. This is possibly enforced by Martin’s mumbling conversations (witnessed by Fermin) with himself while imprisoned in The Prisoner of Heaven. If it is all in David’s mind, then he’s the one who killed his Publisher’s, not Corelli. <br /><br />Or it’s possible Corelli used David as a puppet and committed the murders through him and then made him forget them. This might be supported by the moment when David saves Isabella and then leaves her attackers in the alley. He hears later that they were beaten with a pipe, just like the one he was carrying. So that indicates he might have done it but then blocked it out, Fight Club-style. There are so many possibilities!<br /><br />Another indicator that Corelli really is the Devil, regardless of whether or not others can see him; the first author who lived in the Tower House went through the same thing David did. If it’s all in David’s head then the other author’s story wouldn’t make sense. And we see Christina go crazy and speak to an invisible person, which once again suggests that Corelli is there. <br /><br />So my conclusion in the end is that I think it’s a combination of both things. I think it is madness, but I think it’s caused by Corelli who really is the Devil. He uses the madness as a weapon to get what he wants from people. <br /><br />**SPOILERS OVER**<br /><br />I was forewarned by other fans not to rush through The Angel’s Game, as I was tempted to do. Zafon is an author that should be savored. His novels are so full of his passion for both Barcelona and reading that I found myself wishing I could wander the city's streets after I put the book down. I wish so badly that the Cemetery of Forgotten Books was a real place Now that I have re-read this one I feel like I’ve noticed so many more important details and I understand it much better. I have a feeling my appreciation for it will deepen each time I return to it. <br /><br />BOTTOM LINE: A beautifully twisted and strange novel, The Angel’s Game will leave you reeling and wanting to start it all over again when you finish. The complicated plot isn’t for everyone, but it’s worth it if you loved The Shadow of the Wind. If you read and enjoy that one then I would recommend both The Angel's Game and The Prisoner of Heaven. <br /><br />“We looked at each other bound by an infinite complicity that needed no words.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="15814941362994881062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="TL " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4342402-tl"><img alt="TL " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587334107p2/4342402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TL " class="user" itemprop="url" name="TL " href="/user/show/4342402-tl">TL </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4342402-tl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419475505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9414072625430983108"><i>“Every book has a soul, the soul of the person who wrote it and the soul of those who read it and dream about it.” </i><br/>----<br/><br/><i>“We spend a good part of our lives dreaming, especially when we're awake.” </i><br/><br/><i>" A writer never forgets the first time he accepted a few coins or a word of praise in exchange for a story. He will never forget the sweet poison of vanity in his blood and the belief that, if he succeeds in not letting anyone discover his lack of talent, the dream of literature will provide him with a r</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9414072625430983108" style="display:none"><i>“Every book has a soul, the soul of the person who wrote it and the soul of those who read it and dream about it.” </i><br />----<br /><br /><i>“We spend a good part of our lives dreaming, especially when we're awake.” </i><br /><br /><i>" A writer never forgets the first time he accepted a few coins or a word of praise in exchange for a story. He will never forget the sweet poison of vanity in his blood and the belief that, if he succeeds in not letting anyone discover his lack of talent, the dream of literature will provide him with a roof over his head, a hot meal at the end of the day, and what he covets the most: his name printed on a miserable piece of paper that will surely outlive him. A writer is condemned to remember that moment, because from then on he is doomed and his soul has a price." </i><br /><br /><br /><i>"I could have left, chosen any other tome from among the hundreds of thousands, and abandoned that place, never to return. I almost thought I had done just that, as I walked back through the tunnels and corridors of the labyrinth, until I became aware of the book in my hands, like a parasite stuck to my skin. For a split second the idea crossed my mind that the book had a greater desire to leave the place than I did." </i><br /><br /><br /><i>"I dreamed that I was traveling in a train made of black bones, its coaches shaped like coffins, crossing a deserted Barcelona that was strewn with discarded clothes, as if the bodies that had occupied them had simply evaporated. A wasteland of abandoned hats and dresses, suits and shoes that covered the silent streets. The engine gave off a trail of scarlet smoke that spread across the sky like spilled paint."</i><br /><br /><br />I could quote this whole thing haha.. took my time with this, wanting to savor each and every word. Mister Zafon's writing &lt;3! I can't say anything new than what I've said before but I will say it again... simply gorgeous:) <br /><br />This a haunting story and some of the time you are not completely sure what is happening... whether David is crazy or not, what the deal with 'the boss' is, what really happened with Marlasca and the fire with those snake publishers... you just get caught up in everything and time slips away. <br /><br />This is the second book but all the events take place before 'Shadow of the Wind'... it made me smile then and now to spot the little connections of people and things that pop up in that one as well. Especially when you know what will happen to certain people and how it shaped their loved ones.<br /><br />Cemetery of Forgotten books: I would love to live there, make the trek to donate books, pick one myself *happy sigh* A whole book about it would so lovely, so much history you can feel in the place as you walk with those who walk its many paths.<br /><br />Would highly recommend this and any of Mister Zafon's work *waves* happy reading!<br /></span>

<div id="review_311568937" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311568937" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311568937?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781415963043" href="/book/show/8132650-the-angel-s-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311568937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3593875303508261168"><br/>I am a patient reader. I can cope with ambiguity and digression. I enjoy ornate prose and the occasional serving of melodrama. I don't need each and every element of a plot spelled out for me. This means that I loved (almost) every over-the-top melodramatic moment of the first in Carlos Ruiz Zafon's "Cemetery of Lost Books" series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_' title='The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a>. Reading that novel, I was carried away to Barcelona during the Spanish Civil War and thoroughly enjoyed Ruiz Zafon's magical prose. <br/><br/>My overwhe</span>
  <span id="freeText3593875303508261168" style="display:none"><br />I am a patient reader. I can cope with ambiguity and digression. I enjoy ornate prose and the occasional serving of melodrama. I don't need each and every element of a plot spelled out for me. This means that I loved (almost) every over-the-top melodramatic moment of the first in Carlos Ruiz Zafon's "Cemetery of Lost Books" series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a>. Reading that novel, I was carried away to Barcelona during the Spanish Civil War and thoroughly enjoyed Ruiz Zafon's magical prose. <br /><br />My overwhelmingly positive experience of <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> means that I really looked forward to reading this novel. Set some twenty years before <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>, it focuses on a young writer of sensationalist crime novels, David Martin, who is commissioned by a stranger to write a book and finds himself drawn into a nightmarish world where nothing is what it seems to be. It starts out well. Ruiz Zafon creates a sinister, threatening atmosphere within the architectural splendour of Barcelona. David Martin is an interesting character, as is the main antagonist, who may or may not be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lucifer incarnate <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There are discussions of religion, the importance of books and reading and the nature of love. <br /><br />However, it all falls apart at about the halfway point. There's too much ambiguity and digression and too much melodrama. By the end, I had no idea what was going on and what's worse, I didn't much care. I listened to the audiobook edition (which is very well narrated by Dan Stevens) and it occurred to me that my loss of both focus and interest may not have occurred had I been reading the novel rather than listening to it. But I'm not really convinced that's so. <br /><br />It's not as if the novel has nothing going for it. The prose is great, the translation by Lucia Graves is excellent (at least, I assume it is, because it reads like a book written in English) and the threatening, rather Gothic atmosphere Ruiz Zafon creates jump off the page. Four stars for these aspects of the novel and two for the messy, confusing and overblown plot leaves an average of three. <br /><br />I'll definitely go on to read the third book in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13623012.The_Prisoner_of_Heaven__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___3_" title="The Prisoner of Heaven (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #3) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Heaven</a>, if for no other reason than I'm hoping it will explain what this novel was all about. Thank you to Jemidar for accompanying me on the journey. The fact that both of us were confused makes me feel better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3593875303508261168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=2018-aty-challenge">2018-aty-challenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638062641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14622309715179809107">I’ll say one thing for Carlos Ruiz Zafon, you never think you would like to lay his books aside while you are reading them. He presents you with one mystery after another and little clues and pieces that you <i>know</i> are going to figure into the story later but can never imagine how. I find it amazing that anyone could begin to conceive to such complex storylines.<br/><br/>David Martin, an aspiring writer, finds himself embroiled in a very complicated web of evil and sometimes supernatural occurrences, and pa</span>
  <span id="freeText14622309715179809107" style="display:none">I’ll say one thing for Carlos Ruiz Zafon, you never think you would like to lay his books aside while you are reading them. He presents you with one mystery after another and little clues and pieces that you <i>know</i> are going to figure into the story later but can never imagine how. I find it amazing that anyone could begin to conceive to such complex storylines.<br /><br />David Martin, an aspiring writer, finds himself embroiled in a very complicated web of evil and sometimes supernatural occurrences, and part of the fun is trying to determine whether what he is experiencing is “real” in terms of his perceptions. Is he dealing with people? Devils? Is he imagining things? Can any of this be explained in a way that will make sense to anyone besides David? Are people at risk just because they care about him? And, if he is fighting the devil, can he win?<br /><br />I like having a riddle to solve and I can appreciate a clever and intelligent riddler. Not quite as good as The Shadow of the Wind, but close. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14622309715179809107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3434103125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3434103125" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3434103125?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=spooky">spooky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=books-in-translation">books-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3434103125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4256514571610045286">Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br/><br/><b>For close to a decade I’ve thought that <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> was one of the most brilliant novels I had ever read. I had no idea that it was a preamble, setting up for an even bigger story.</b> And I truly believe that <i>The Angel’s Game</i> just scratched the surface; I can feel in my bones that there’s far more to come. I’ve also been reliably informed by TS and Petrik that all of the questions I found left frustratingly open at the end of this book will indeed be answered late</span>
  <span id="freeText4256514571610045286" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5 stars<br /><br /><b>For close to a decade I’ve thought that <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i> was one of the most brilliant novels I had ever read. I had no idea that it was a preamble, setting up for an even bigger story.</b> And I truly believe that <i>The Angel’s Game</i> just scratched the surface; I can feel in my bones that there’s far more to come. I’ve also been reliably informed by TS and Petrik that all of the questions I found left frustratingly open at the end of this book will indeed be answered later in the series, which does nothing but add to my excitement.<br /><blockquote>“Poetry is written with tears, novels with blood, and history with invisible ink.”</blockquote><br />In this book we meet David Martín, an orphan who yearns to be a writer. Thanks to his mentor, Pedro Vidal, Martín is given his chance. But when his writing career takes an unexpected trajectory, he finds himself making a deal with the devil and mirroring the tragic history of another. At its core, Martín’s story is one of intriguing mystery and gothic horror. <b>The atmosphere of this novel was so creepy that I often couldn’t tell if there was a supernatural element to it or if the eeriness was due exclusively to the lush, dark setting.</b> That question wasn’t truly answered, even in the final pages, though its answer was alluded to. I loved the balance Zafón struck between reality and the supernatural; it definitely kept me on my toes.<br /><blockquote>“Inspiration comes when you stick your elbows on the table, your bottom on the chair and you start sweating. Choose a theme, an idea, and squeeze your brain until it hurts. That’s called inspiration.”</blockquote><br /><i>The Angel’s Game</i> was radically different in tone than its predecessor, The Shadow of the Wind, but that made the Martín’s search for answers even more compelling. <b>Where The Shadow of the Wind was a historical fiction literary mystery, <i>The Angel’s Game</i> is, as stated above, a gothic horror, though there is plenty of mystery and romance and even magical realism in its pages.</b> While I truly loved the atmosphere of the book, and have rarely come across such lush descriptions of setting, the mystery was what truly kept me reading. I was dying to know how Martín’s story would tie into Daniel Sempere’s tale, and finally gaining that information was incredibly satisfying.<br /><blockquote>“The only way you can truly get to know an author is through the trail of ink he leaves behind him; the person you think you see is only an empty character: truth is always hidden in fiction.”</blockquote><br />Probably my least favorite element of this book was the central romance. If it can even be considered central. <b>Martín’s romantic interest came across as incredibly two-dimensional, in my opinion, and seemed to only be there to drive the plot forward instead of serving as a character in her own right.</b> I’m not a fan of damsels as plot devices, and that’s truly what she felt like. I know Zafón can pen wonderful female characters, as he demonstrates beautifully in another character in this novel, so I know he could have done better with this particular woman. Besides that, <u>I really have no other complaints about this novel</u>. Especially since, as I mentioned earlier, TS and Petrik assured me that my questions would be answer in the next two novels. <br /><blockquote>“Sooner or later, the word becomes flesh and the flesh bleeds.”</blockquote><br /><b>As with <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>, my very favorite element of <i>The Angel’s Game</i> was the role of books, both in plot and setting. </b> Sempere and Sons remains one of the coziest bookshops I’ve come across in fiction, and I wish I could live there. Then you have The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, after which this entire series is named. There’s something so magical about the idea of the Cemetery, and as well as about its role as a setting. <b>The thought of a nearly endless labyrinth of books, whose authors and existences have been lost to society, hidden deep within a city, is enchanting.</b> <u>It also provides a beautiful continuity between the novels, and the repetition of dialogue regarding it lends a reverence and awe to the Cemetery’s existence that moves me</u>. <br /><blockquote>“This place is a mystery. A sanctuary. Every book, every volume you see, has a soul. The soul of the person who wrote it and the should of those who read it and lived and dreamed with it. Every time a book changes hands, every time someone runs his eyes down its pages, its spirit grows and strengthens. In this place, books no longer remembered by anyone, books that are lost in time, live forever, waiting for the day when they will reach a new reader’s hands, a new spirit…”</blockquote><br /><b>Zafón also has profound things to say about books themselves, the art of writing, and even the impact story has on religion and philosophy and psychology, all of which I found fascinating. </b> And once again, <u>both the writing and the translation of it are absolutely <i>stunning</i></u>. This is a book that begs to be annotated. Since I couldn’t bring myself to mark in my lovely physical copy, I borrowed an electronic copy from the library for the express purpose of taking notes.<br /><blockquote>“We think we understand a song’s lyrics, but what makes us believe in them, or not, is the music.”</blockquote><br />I’m so glad I was persuaded to read beyond <i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>. As much as I adore that novel, it’s so exciting to see how much more there is to the story. If the third and fourth installments maintain this level of craftsmanship, <i>The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</i> will undoubtedly become one of my favorite series. <b><i>The Angel’s Game</i> made me think and question and laugh and feel, and I honestly can’t wait to see what else Zafón’s world has in store.</b><br /><br /><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-25S" rel="nofollow noopener"> this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4256514571610045286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1738462700156395079" style="display:none">I absolutely loved The Shadow of the Wind and expected this book to be my favorite book of the year. Perhaps my expectations were too high to give it a fair chance. I didn't care for the story. I rarely felt like picking the book up after taking a break but continued to think that there would be some redeeming aspect as I read and was closer to the end. I would not recommend this book- it was terrible. I lent it to a friend and she didn't even bother finishing it (she reads a couple hundred books each year and has only given up on a book four or five times). I'm sad to say that this book is nothing like the great Shadow of the Wind. </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4763999-beatrix?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer255521157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7407248875413602503"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Everything is a tale, Martin. What we believe, what we know, what we remember, even what we dream. Everything is a story, a narrative, a sequence of events with characters communicating an emotional content. We only accept as true what can be narrated.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Zafón’s books are pure magic. And while I loved <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_' title='The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a>
</i> because of the story, I enjoyed <i>The Angel’s Game</i> primarily because of its protagonist, David Martin.<br/><br/>I really can’t properly describe why I love Zafón as a writer</span>
  <span id="freeText7407248875413602503" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Everything is a tale, Martin. What we believe, what we know, what we remember, even what we dream. Everything is a story, a narrative, a sequence of events with characters communicating an emotional content. We only accept as true what can be narrated.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Zafón’s books are pure magic. And while I loved <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a>
</i> because of the story, I enjoyed <i>The Angel’s Game</i> primarily because of its protagonist, David Martin.<br /><br />I really can’t properly describe why I love Zafón as a writer; you truly need to read him to understand. His words are so powerful, and his books so atmospheric; when I’m reading one of his books I feel like I belong to that Barcelona of the early 20th century. To me, he’s special because he so skillfully combines genres. In fact, I’d dare say that Zafón <b>transcends genres</b>, his books belong to a category of their own. Here you’ll find it all: <b>history, tragedy, mystery, romance, comedy</b>…<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Every work of art is aggressive, Isabella. And every artist's life is a small war or a large one, beginning with oneself and one's limitations. To achieve anything you must first have ambition and then talent, knowledge, and finally the opportunity.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Now, there are two main reasons why I loved this book so much and two tiny little things that bothered me. First the good; the <b>writing</b> is simply <b>remarkable</b>. I loved the pacing, the dialogues, the characters. I love the fact that despite this being a gothic novel, it doesn’t lack humor. The second reason is the protagonist – David Martin. I loved him even more than Daniel Sempere, from <i>the Shadow</i>. <br /><br />Furthermore, what I didn’t like that much was the forced love story between Cristina and David. I personally found no sparks between the two and I thought Cristina was so grumpy and moody. On the other hand, I absolutely loved <b>Isabella</b>. Her conversations with David (her Mr. Rochester) were among my favorites in the novel. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Life had taught her that we all require big and small lies in order to survive, just as much as we need air. She used to say that if during one single day, from dawn to dusk, we could see the naked reality of the world, and of ourselves, we would either take our own lives or lose our minds.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This book touches upon magical realism at times, and if, like me, you’re generally not the biggest fan, I think it’s better to be prepared beforehand – you might not get all the answers after you finish this book. <br /><br />And finally, that <b>ending</b> needs to be addressed. I can see why some readers were left confused and thought the ending was ambiguous and unsatisfactory. I have to agree that the last 100 pages were not as good as the rest of the novel; I loved the build-up, but I believe the novel could’ve been wrapped up more nicely. Who is in fact Andreas Corelli? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Is he an angel or the devil? Or perhaps just a fragment of Martin’s imagination? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Nevertheless, the story does not end here. All three books from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/72526-el-cementerio-de-los-libros-olvidados " rel="nofollow noopener">The Cemetery of Forgotten Books</a> are related. Now, having read <i>the Angel</i>, some things from <i>the Shadow</i> are clearer to me; just as you will fully understand this book (and Martin’s fate) if you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13623012.The_Prisoner_of_Heaven__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___3_" title="The Prisoner of Heaven (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #3) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Heaven</a> too. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If you must know now: we learn that Martin is mentally unstable, and I think that here he was a unreliable narrator of sorts. Corelli might not have even been real. And we also realize just how strong his and Isabella’s friendship had been. I really wanted the two of them together…but, that ship has sailed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In conclusion, I’d wholeheartedly recommend this book (and any other by Zafón) to everyone who loves books, who lives and breathes them. With his books you will feel at home and be reminded as to why you read; because as he says: <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Truth is always hidden in fiction.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7407248875413602503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2354068080" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2354068080" />
    <a title="Diane " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/143168-diane"><img alt="Diane " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558395550p2/143168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2354068080?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane " href="/user/show/143168-diane">Diane </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=challenge-2019">challenge-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=goodreads-joint-read">goodreads-joint-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=own-already">own-already</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=owned-forever">owned-forever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354068080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3187029895716831821">This is a hard book for me to rate and review. The writing, of course, was exquisite, always to be expected from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/815.Carlos_Ruiz_Zaf_n' title='Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carlos Ruiz Zafón</a>. And I certainly enjoyed reading what was a prequel, timewise, to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_' title='The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Shadow of the Wind</a>, but the primary storyline of this one was just not something I could fully grasp, understand, follow or believe. It had a supernatural 'spell' thrown into the mix which just wasn't my cup of tea. I have to say, though, that it takes a brilliant writer to come up with this; in ad</span>
  <span id="freeText3187029895716831821" style="display:none">This is a hard book for me to rate and review. The writing, of course, was exquisite, always to be expected from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/815.Carlos_Ruiz_Zaf_n" title="Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">Carlos Ruiz Zafón</a>. And I certainly enjoyed reading what was a prequel, timewise, to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a>, but the primary storyline of this one was just not something I could fully grasp, understand, follow or believe. It had a supernatural 'spell' thrown into the mix which just wasn't my cup of tea. I have to say, though, that it takes a brilliant writer to come up with this; in addition to tying it into a series. <br /><br />So while I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1232.The_Shadow_of_the_Wind__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___1_" title="The Shadow of the Wind (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #1) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Wind</a> was near perfect, in fact I read it twice, this one fell short. But I plan to continue with the series and am looking forward to getting back to Daniel, Bea and the other characters in the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13623012.The_Prisoner_of_Heaven__The_Cemetery_of_Forgotten_Books___3_" title="The Prisoner of Heaven (The Cemetery of Forgotten Books, #3) by Carlos Ruiz Zafón" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prisoner of Heaven</a>.<br /><br />Joint read with NI friends, Susan and Sarah. Glad to have finally read it since I've owned it since 2009. How embarrassing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3187029895716831821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2994991396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2994991396" />
    <a title="Mattia Ravasi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14579657-mattia-ravasi"><img alt="Mattia Ravasi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584813562p2/14579657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2994991396?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mattia Ravasi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mattia Ravasi" href="/user/show/14579657-mattia-ravasi">Mattia Ravasi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2994991396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6544973700110220173"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RMzJwT-dW6g' rel='nofollow noopener'>Series review</a><br/><br/>If The Shadow of the Wind was Zafon's thrilling take on metafictional bibliophile fiction a la Eco, Calvino or Borges, Angel's Game is an uncanny Gothic tale in the tradition of Hoffmann and pre-cosmic Lovecraft. It doesn't pack the same amount of sheer love of literature that seeps through the sentences of Wind (although there's plenty of that here, too), but in terms of plot and thrills it might be even more engaging.<br/><br/>I can see the ending as especially divisive - I adored it, but i</span>
  <span id="freeText6544973700110220173" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RMzJwT-dW6g" rel="nofollow noopener">Series review</a><br /><br />If The Shadow of the Wind was Zafon's thrilling take on metafictional bibliophile fiction a la Eco, Calvino or Borges, Angel's Game is an uncanny Gothic tale in the tradition of Hoffmann and pre-cosmic Lovecraft. It doesn't pack the same amount of sheer love of literature that seeps through the sentences of Wind (although there's plenty of that here, too), but in terms of plot and thrills it might be even more engaging.<br /><br />I can see the ending as especially divisive - I adored it, but it's the kind of conclusion certain readers are bound to despise, and not necessarily for bad reasons.<br /><br />Must read for fans of Wind, or for people looking for an engaging novel in a Gothic vein.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6544973700110220173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AHSbs9xyQkf/wXUsi/SKNkXzF8uxGP+hEcE2nmmIVOcj8ce4hutJcC+S1ELCJEec2j+1SPrkDtPXKD5qPQSquQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_54984'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54984.La_catedral_del_mar?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">La catedral del mar (La catedral del mar, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/31003.Ildefonso_Falcones?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Ildefonso Falcones<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.11 avg rating &mdash; 39,967 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2006\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer6149814571673966594\">Siglo XIV. La ciudad de Barcelona se encuentra en su momento de mayor prosperidad; ha crecido hacia la Ribera, el humilde barrio de los pescadores, cuyos habitantes deciden construir, con el dinero de unos y el esfuerzo de otros, el mayor templo mari<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6149814571673966594\" style=\"display:none\">Siglo XIV. La ciudad de Barcelona se encuentra en su momento de mayor prosperidad; ha crecido hacia la Ribera, el humilde barrio de los pescadores, cuyos habitantes deciden construir, con el dinero de unos y el esfuerzo de otros, el mayor templo mariano jamás conocido: Santa María de la Mar.\n\nUna construcción que es paralela a la azarosa historia de Arnau, un siervo de la tierra que huye de los abusos de su señor feudal y se refugia en Barcelona, donde se convierte en ciudadano y, con ello, en hombre libre.\n\nEl joven Arnau trabaja como palafrenero, estibador, soldado y cambista. Una vida extenuante, siempre al amparo de la catedral de la mar, que le iba a llevar de la miseria del fugitivo a la nobleza y la riqueza. Pero con esta posición privilegiada también le llega la envidia de sus pares, que urden una sórdida conjura que pone su vida en manos de la Inquisición...\n\n&quot;La catedral del mar&quot; es una trama en la que se entrecruzan lealtad y venganza, traición y amor, guerra y peste, en un mundo marcado por la intolerancia religiosa, la ambición material y la segregación social. Es una novela de amor y es una novela que al final termina por brindar esperanza. «Una novela polifónica que narra con intensidad y con excepcional dinamismo una historia de violencia en el México contemporáneo donde el amor y la redención aún son posibles. El autor se sirve tantode una extraordinaria fuerza visual como de la recreación y reinvención del lenguaje coloquial para lograr una obra de inquietante verosimilitud. Los distintos planos narrativos tienen como hilo conductor el cuerpo humano, motivo de celebración y expuesto a numerosos excesos.»Del acta del jurado La crítica ha dicho:«El mexicano Guillermo Arriaga no es solo un escritor de la gran pantalla sino un narrador de raza, cuyas obsesiones vitales dejan honda huella en el lector.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Un autor absolutamente único.»Guadalupe Nettel «Uno de los autores contemporáneos más potentes, intensos y originales de la literatura en idioma español.»El Exprés (México) «Arriaga demuestra ser gran director a la par que gran escritor.»Roberto Piorno, Guía del Ocio «Con sensibilidad extrema y poderío visual, enlazando con coherencia personajes y situaciones que inicialmente parecen no guardar relación [...], Arriaga demuestra que, además de un espléndido guionista, también es un buen director.»Carlos Boyero, El País «El Salvaje es uno de los mejores libros que he leído, no solo en este sino en los últimos años.»Santiago Gamboa «La presencia ominosa de la muerte; el amor o la pasión que todo lo crea y, por encima, la fuerza irrefrenable de la vida que arrastra todo consigo en su prepotencia arrolladora. Esos son los motivos que entrelaza con sabiduría en El Salvaje, una ambiciosa y lograda novela.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Sublime Arriaga. El Salvaje consagra a su autor como el mejor escritor mexicano actual y como una figura indiscutible de las letras universales. [...] No os lo penséis y leedlo: vuestro espíritu os lo agradeceráGabri Ródenas, Zenda Libros «Su novela más ambiciosa y extensa, de estructura compleja e impregnada de elementos personales, en la que su personaje, Juan Guillermo, pese a las más terribles pérdidas, es capaz de reconstruir su vida.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14633539169237915457\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; Los musulmanes, cuya presencia tenía ochocientos años de antigüedad, se ven convertidos en una minoría oprimida económicamente y humillada en sus costumbres y religión, que incluso son obligados a abandonar.Hartos de tanta injusticia, los moriscos, que es como se llamaba a los musulmanes españoles, se alzan en los montes de Granada contra los cristianos y emprenden una lucha desigual. Entre los sublevados está Hernando, hijo de una morisca y del sacerdote que la había violado; ello hace que sea rechazado, tanto por los suyos debido a su origen, como por los cristianos, por la cultura y costumbres de su madre. Hernando busca libertad y respeto, pero se encuentra con la brutalidad de unos y otros. También descubre el amor, en la persona de la valerosa Fátima, la de los hermosos ojos negros.Tras la derrota de la insurrección, Hernando es deportado a la ciudad de Córdoba, la hermosa ciudad que aún conserva el legado de su pasado árabe. En ella Hernando intenta comenzar una nueva vida, que será una nueva etapa en la lucha por la tolerancia y la concordia entre las dos culturas.El autor de La catedral del mar vuelve con una trepidante novela con las mismas claves que llevaron al éxito a la primera: fidelidad histórica entrecruzada con un conmovedor relato de amor y odio, de ilusiones perdidas y esperanzas que dan sentido a la vida <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1267929833421179752">Carlos Ruiz Zafón was a Spanish novelist. Born in Barcelona in 1964, he lived in Los Ángeles, United States, since 1994, and worked as a scriptwriter aside from writing novels.<br/><br/>His first novel, <i>El príncipe de la niebla</i> (<i>The Prince of Mist</i>, 1993), earned the Edebé literary prize for young adult fiction. He is also the author of three more young-adult novels, <i>El palacio de la medianoche</i> (1994), <i>Las l</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1267929833421179752" style="display:none">Carlos Ruiz Zafón was a Spanish novelist. Born in Barcelona in 1964, he lived in Los Ángeles, United States, since 1994, and worked as a scriptwriter aside from writing novels.<br /><br />His first novel, <i>El príncipe de la niebla</i> (<i>The Prince of Mist</i>, 1993), earned the Edebé literary prize for young adult fiction. He is also the author of three more young-adult novels, <i>El palacio de la medianoche</i> (1994), <i>Las luces de septiembre</i> (1995) and <i>Marina</i> (1999).<br /><br />In 2001 he published the novel <i>La sombra del viento</i> (<i>The Shadow of the Wind</i>), his first 'adult' novel, which has sold millions of copies worldwide. Since its publication, <i>La sombra del viento</i> has garnered critical acclaim around the world and has won numerous international awards. Ruiz Zafón's works have been published in more than 40 countries and have been translated into more than 30 languages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1267929833421179752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
